\chapter{Word lists}
\label{Para_A}
This appendix presents 2,215 lexemes which form the basis for the phonological analysis in \chapref{Para_2}.\footnote{The 2,215 lexemes are extracted from the 2,458-item list, discussed in §\ref{Para_1.11.6}. The remaining 243 items include lexemes \isi{historically derived} by (unproductive) \isi{affixation} of loanwords, such as \textitbf{berkomunikasi} ‘communicate’ as well as collocations such as \textitbf{ade-kaka} ‘siblings’ (see §\ref{Para_3.1} and §\ref{Para_3.2}, respectively).} Included are 1,117 Papuan Malay lexical roots, listed in Appendix \ref{Para_A.1} (see also §\ref{Para_2.1}), and 719 loanwords, listed in Appendix \ref{Para_A.2} (see also §\ref{Para_2.5}). Also included are 380 items, \isi{historically derived} by (unproductive) \isi{affixation} of Malay roots, listed in Appendix \ref{Para_A.3} (see also §\ref{Para_2.4.4.2}). Upon further investigation some of the words listed as inherited Papuan Malay lexemes in Appendix \ref{Para_A.1} and Appendix \ref{Para_A.3} may also turn out to be loanwords.

The lexemes listed in the following sections are presented in their alphabetical order. For each lexeme the following details are included: their phonetic transcription, word class, and English gloss. As discussed in §\ref{Para_2.4.4} and §\ref{Para_2.5.3.3}, lexical roots in Papuan Malay typically carry penultimate stress. In the following sections, lexemes which do not have penultimate but ultimate or antepenultimate stress are marked with “x” for easier recognition.

\section{Loanwords}
\label{Para_A.2}
\begin{longtable}{lllp{1.75cm}p{4.25cm}}

& \textitbf{abadi} & \textstyleChCharisSIL{a.ˈba.di} & \textsc{v.mo(st)} & be eternal\\
